Hey, Dave, enjoyed the review especially your honest comment about how outrageously expensive they are. I'm due for an upgrade and I'm looking at a loaded 16" about $4200. What I love is how well they are built. I actually still use a Macbook Pro 17" loaded and upgraded with an SSD, but, it's time to move on because the OS is getting real old on this one. My 17" was also loaded. I paid $3500 for it, years ago. The way I justified it, then, was Boot Camp. I have a lot of Windows software (to replace the software would be expensive) so, I do a lot of video/audio rendering on the Windows side with Vegas and Sound Forge Pro and other tools. For the reason of performance, I did not go virtual with Parallels and just used the MAC as a Windows computer booting into it and it's been great. I also don't like how the new Parallels is a subscription, so, to create a Windows virtual out of Parallels, I'd have to pay $100 a year forever and when the price goes up, even more, just for the privilege of using my Windows virtual. So, my question is, all this mentioned, I justified the large expense of the Mac 17" because it was 2-computers in 1. I didn't need a 2nd high end Windows computer. Now, if I buy the new MAC, obviously I have to deal with Parallels and a subscription, which sucks, but, here's the dealbreaker. Will Parallels give me the performance in virtual running intensive programs like CAD, Vegas, Sound Forge, etc. or will I be disappointed. I even have old Adobe software I bought when it was sold that still works great. So, will I be disappointed in virtual running those kind of programs or will I also have to consider replacing all that older software which really makes this a dealbreaker.  What do you think? I really don't want refurbished, but, I guess I could find a loaded 16" with that intel processor that would last several years, too. Or, I could just say, "see ya later" and just buy a loaded Dell XPS 17" or even a Dell Workstation model and it will run all my Windows stuff and just move on? What do you think? No matter what I do, I am going to have to run some Windows programs. I just have too many programs in Windows to just replace everything and go MAC, but, I do love Final Cut and having both operating systems and the benefits of syncing with IPAD, a phone and all of that but, the prices are just insane. The other thing that is so frustrating is the older Macbook Pro 17" was fully upgradable. It didn't come maxed out on RAM or with an SSD and I was able to get in the game for $3500 and upgrade the machine, later on. With the memory not being able to be upgraded anymore, you have no choice but to go all the way when you buy it. After all, I don't want to get 16gig ram or 32gig ram or a 500gig hard drive and then kick myself because I can't uprade it and have to buy a new computer. Really sucks they way they design them so they cannot be upgraded later. If you buy a new car and you want to add an accessory or upgrade the stock OEM tires, you can. But, not on a MAC. Anyway, your thoughts appreciated.

I am still trying to figure out if the m1 max would even be able to compete for 3D task. And I'm left with a what was Apple thinking. So the GPU sits between a mobile 3060 and 3070. So assuming it could match cuda performance in cycles because that is the only data i can actually readily find benchmark data for. Like I know redshift has been optimized for metal but I haven't been able to find any actual benchmarks and the only thing I've seen is annecdotal evidence of some guy saying hey we went from 20 minutes per render to 40 s followed by videos after that article showing minutes per render. But without actual benchmarks it's hard to tell. But assuming metal in cycles x matches cuda which is a big if a m1 max should take 3.1x the time to render as a 16GB mobile 3080 or a mobile A5000 due to Nvidia having ray accelerators. So if you are a Character modeler, annimator, texture artist, even a game environment artist PC is 3x faster and you aren't likely to exceed the 16 GB frame buffer. Now if you are one of the guys going over 16GB you are likely in the movie industry and looking at the full scene at which point 64 GB just isn't enough I mean there were some industry professionals speculating that the 256GB on threadrippper systems might not be enough. Yeah I dunno. I would be more optimistic if I could find redshift benchmarks using metal showing actual performance but as of right now it's super expensive while not being actually faster. I mean they showed this cool thing with the original enterprise and being able to do a cross-section which was cool but without some way to actually see it or benchmark or something, it's hard to draw conclusions though I imagine some people will buy it all the same and insist it's the best thing since sliced bread.

Apple's next Macbook Pro 16" will be called the M2 THICC.  BTW, going by the scores Dave put up for Cinebench R23, comparing M1 with M1 Max, it's 38% higher score.  Does that translate to generally 38% more performance overall?  In Geekbench 5, an ASUS Zephyrus G15 with 3070 Mobile is either tied with the M1 Max or far exceeds it (there's a great variation in the scores, but most are 100K score range).  That's an $1800 Windows laptop with 165hz screen, 100% DCI-P3.  Hoping to see more M1 Max performance numbers in the coming days as more reviews come out.  But if it's 3060 Mobile performance at best, then while it's a big step forward for Macbooks, you can get comparable performance for considerably less with a G15.

It's two folds: 1. Apple could have gone with a teardrop design instead of a notch, but next year when they do add FaceID, they don't want to move to a notch then. Plus this way, they can shrink the notch from the year they introduce FaceID. 2. Consistent Design Language: The notch has become synonymous with iPhones. You would not mistake it for any other phone in 2021. They want that same unmistakable identity with the Macbooks vs any other laptop.
